Shanghai Newspaper Local Supplement

Talking Points

Reconsider the Ban on Dancing 221

— Shi Ji

The First Special District City Federation has again submitted a petition to the Municipal Government to ban dance halls, reiterating the previous proposal to "maintain social order by rectifying public morals."

The reasons for "petitioning for a ban" are the same as those presented before: "Detailing the four harms and first implementing the two restrictions."

It is commendable that the gentlemen of the City Federation are concerned about "social peace and the future of the entire nation and people," and therefore express disapproval of "the abnormal development of dance halls in Shanghai today, which attract young men and women every night, dancing and singing wildly all night long, and indulging in licentiousness to the extreme," and petition for a ban. However, after expressing our support, we cannot remain silent.

Between the first petition for a ban and this second petition, dance halls have undergone significant changes in the past few months: First, small dance halls charging one yuan for eight dances or ten dances have sprung up like mushrooms after rain; second, dance halls compete with "erotic dances," "conventions," and "mysterious performances" to attract dancers; third, they extend the hours, adding "tea dances" in addition to "evening dances," and even "offering exquisite refreshments" to compete; fourth, in addition to these, what has "abnormally developed" even more recently is the rise of dance schools or dance art research societies that are in fact disguised as cheaper small dance halls. The dancers in these dance schools are mostly junior employees of general stores. From these phenomena, we can see that dancing has spread from gentlemen and ladies and wealthy youths to the common people. However, now that dancing has become a popular hobby among the general public, if we pay close attention to the situation in the dance halls, we can discover two other things: the so-called "observers" sitting in the dance halls who do not dance are much more numerous than the dancers, and although new dance halls seem to spring up like mushrooms after rain, those that close down one after another are also numerous.

From the above facts, we can also see the "ever-declining" state of dance halls. Why are dance halls in an ever-declining state, and yet penetrating into the common people? We only need to think carefully to know that this is not without reason. China is now an era of suffering. Those who cannot bear the torment of this suffering turn to the path of decadent, chronic suicide. For example, many students who recently returned from petitioning vowed on the train that they would spend the rest of their lives in song and dance halls.

This is just one example. Another example is a young man "who once studied in France" reported in the same newspaper, who was sued by a dance hall owner for issuing bad checks because he was "unemployed at home after returning to the country." The youths in this society are either weak and chronically suicidal or strong and "taking risks!"

The method of treating the head when the head hurts and treating the foot when the foot hurts is only conceived by mediocre doctors when they have no other choice; moreover, this is still the method of "cutting off the head when the head hurts!"

As for the issue of the future of the dance girls and those who depend on dance halls for a living after the ban on dancing, that is secondary.

Departure 222

— Especially

—Returning Home in Bitter Snow, Part 5

This long line, like a snake, lay on the snowy ground. Except for the lead car, the rest were without roofs. This so-called lead car was not like an ordinary passenger car; on the Beijing-Shanghai line, it would just be a baggage car.

Of course, it wouldn’t have any windows. Two iron doors were separated at both ends of the car, and inside was one large, undivided compartment!

So, we spread out our mats and nailed them to the iron plates on top. We did the same on the opposite side, just barely leaving a rectangular opening for entry and exit. In this way, the large compartment was divided into three sections. The southern side was occupied by our group, the other side by several attendants from the arena. And what about the passageway in the middle? Several friends in distress, whose names we didn't know, also moved in under a sense of sorrow.

After lunch, everyone's boxes and baskets were brought onto the car. The remaining mats were spread flat on the iron plates like carpets. Luggage was spread out without any particular order, and the boxes were piled high in one corner.

The day was really short. It got dark. Zhang Shun came over, lit the kerosene lamp, and casually asked if we wanted anything to eat. Then, he turned and left.

"Come here!" Old Qiu called out to him. "Check if we have enough water. Prepare more hard candy, in case we get delayed on the road!"

For some reason, we always felt that Old Qiu's face didn't look good, as if he had something to worry about.

"Will we actually be able to leave today?" Little Wei said, breaking the calm air.

"Nine o'clock," he said, looking at his watch. "Just wait, there are still three hours."

Listen, the engine in front let out a sound, and then the car moved a little. Perhaps an lonely old mother is waiting for the return of her wandering son? The sound carried a slight message. What shall I use to comfort her heart? Bitterness surged from the depths of my heart straight to my nose. Unable to suppress this painful sorrow, tears fell. But I didn't dare let others see, and I buried my head in the quilt. Alas, how could I not be careful of them resenting this unfortunate action, on the part of a 毛孩子 who is receiving the grace of others!

"Everyone," Old Qiu said to the people in the aisle, "There is something I need to clarify. Riding the car is not a problem, but if something goes wrong on the road, or we encounter an inspection, the responsibility..."

Many eyes looked at Old Qiu, thinking. They didn't say anything. Naturally, what could they say? Relying on the eaves of others, needing the giving of the spring breeze, being terrified—it was simply like creatures trembling on a tightrope. Rather than suffer the attack of fear, it was better to take a chance. They and I shared the same fate!

Soon, the wheels pressed against the thin ice on the tracks. The weather was so cold that people couldn't stretch out their hands.

"I hope this trip goes smoothly and we can return to Tianjin safely!"

Willow 223

— Zhu Mingxia

Originally, a topic like this should be written by someone as erudite as Mr. Zhou Zuoren to produce an outstanding article. Someone as shallow as I am is really "not the right choice." But just as Mr. Zhou Zuoren said, finding a topic is not easy, so I'll still write a little now.

Willow, or just called "Liu," according to legend, Yang Guang opened the Grand Canal and had people plant willows along the banks. Later, when he went down to Yangzhou, the lush shade provided coolness along the way, so he bestowed the surname "Yang" upon them. This legend doesn't seem to be entirely accurate, because in

Nonsense 224

— (Bragging)

On the 13th, the countries that signed the Locarno Treaties met in London. British Foreign Secretary Chamberlain went out first, looking worried. Chancellor of the Exchequer Lord Halifax and Italian Ambassador Grandi followed, also looking concerned. Tan Laosan said that this meeting must have been filled with gloom and sadness, not at all like attending a dance or a viewing party. Why? "Watching others carry burdens doesn't seem hard, but when you put it on your own shoulders, your mouth twists in pain."

Next to the Kunning Palace in the Forbidden City, there are three side rooms that are tightly closed and have never been opened. Even when Puyi left the palace and the Forbidden City Preservation Committee was organized, they were not inspected. The inventory of the Forbidden City doesn't record any antiquities in these rooms. Tan Laosan said that this shows how diligent the members of the Forbidden City Committee are in their work.

Page 18

Before Yang Guang, there were already lines in the classics such as "In the past when I went, the willows were lush," so the name "willow" has "a long history." Naturally, according to those who are knowledgeable in the study of things, "Yang" and "Liu" are originally two different kinds of trees. So, after "In the past when I went, the willows were lush," there is "Now when I return, the rain and snow are heavy." Rain and snow are naturally two different things, and this is certainly correct. But we don't know whether the poets of that time were as concerned with parallelism as later generations, especially since the two characters "rain" and "snow" can also mean "snowing."

Even so, in our hometown, Yang and Liu are indeed two different kinds of trees. Willow droops, while Yang stretches upwards. Naturally, some people say that if you plant a poplar tree upside down, it will become a weeping willow, but in practice, this is not true.

Among all trees (except evergreens), willow is the most characteristic of spring, because it is the first to bud when spring arrives, and it becomes lush and dark green as spring deepens. Because of this, the poet mentioned above used it as a representative of spring, saying "The willows are lush" to hint at spring. Later, even when faced with the helplessness of spring's departure, they hoped to use willow branches to tie it back.

Willows were probably originally a product of the south. "Trees are like this, how can people bear it?" The "like this" tree refers to the willows of southern Hubei. Therefore, in Lao Can's Travels, describing the scenery of Jinan, it is said, "Every house has springs, every household has weeping willows, resembling Jiangnan."

Among all trees, willows are also the easiest to grow. Anything that grows easily is certainly not strong. Therefore, "The weak willow's shape anticipates willow first withering." Taking willow to be mentioned alongside the herbaceous cattail, the ancients said, "It takes ten years to grow a tree." I think that only willow trees can be grown in ten years; at least pine, cypress, elm, and nan trees take at least thirty or forty years. In our hometown, there is even a saying, "A willow tree surrounding a house indicates a newly rich family," saying that if a house is only surrounded by willow trees, it must be a newly rich family, because if it were a family that had been wealthy for generations, it would definitely be surrounded by elm and nan trees.

"Many are planted in Jiangnan near water." This is a statement about willows that has merit. Actually, it's not necessary to plant them near water; they can be planted anywhere, because they grow easily, so they are found everywhere near pavilions and bridges. In ancient times, farewells mostly took place on land at pavilions and by water at bridges. At that time, people would look up and see willow trees, so they would reach out and break off some willow branches to give as farewell gifts, either intentionally or forgetting their horse whips and using them as substitutes. In short, because they were encountered frequently during farewells, willow trees subtly became a symbol of reluctance to part. Naturally, there are countless examples of this.

Willows are green and drooping. Their beauty lies in their swaying grace, and it just so happens that a woman's waist is also considered beautiful when it is slender and swaying. Therefore, poets even compared willows to women's waists. "With golden reins and jade bridles, he gazes in the wind, recognizing Yang's quiet and gentle waist." "Don't let them be moved into the Linghe Palace; three thousand palace maids would be jealous of her." Isn't this good evidence?

Because they "wither first in autumn," autumn willows are even more of a source of sadness for poets. There are countless autumn willow poems from ancient times; I won't mention them all here. Bai Shidaoren's ci poems are rare masterpieces throughout the ages. In "Wretched Grief," he has the following lines:

"In the alleys of Hefei, willows are planted everywhere. In the autumn wind at dusk, they rustle softly. When I lived there, with my door closed, I heard the neighing of a horse. I went out of the city and looked around, and all I saw was desolate smoke and wild grass, an unbearable sadness."

Although this doesn't specifically talk about autumn willows, everything he describes truly captures the spirit of autumn willows. This, along with "Trees are like this," can probably be considered the two greatest writings on "willow"!

There is a willow tree outside the window. Although the spring is as cold as water, there are already some sprouts in this continuous spring rain. Around Qingming and Hanshi, there will probably be many children climbing and breaking off tender branches to make willow balls. "Wearing willows on Qingming" — I am immersed in a sea of memories again. The rain keeps falling.

Nora says, "I don’t believe it. Does the law not allow a daughter to find a way to prevent her dying father from being worried? Does the law not allow a wife to save her husband's life? If so, this must be a stupid law!"

Krogstad says coldly, "The law doesn't care about a person's intentions."

The orchestra of the troupe is strong and can be called the best in Shanghai. There are a total of eight members, all of whom are leading figures in Shanghai's musical groups. "Rose Marie" 231

This opera, "Rose Marie," which moved the world ten years ago, was originally a musical opera produced in 1924 by the great playwright Arthur Hammerstein. When it was performed at the Imperial Theatre in New York, it was a great success and lasted for two years. It was re-edited in 1927. Now, MGM has starred in it with the silver screen darlings Jeanette MacDonald and Nelson Eddy and directed by W. S. Van Dyke. The music and songs in the film are all guided and created by the famous American musicians Rudolf Friml and Herbert Stothart. Therefore, the famous songs in the film, such as the Indian "Indian Love Call", "Rose Marie", and Shakespeare's "Romeo and Juliet", are all extremely precious. The totem pole dance, sincere open history of wonders, is blessed to those who love music and movies.

President Wang of the "Little" Lan Jun in "The Beauty of the Flowers and Leaves"
